  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7d91274a-48f2-4d13-a25e-ff5f8736af99'
      });

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText6056555751924677027" style="display:none">Juliette escaped from The Reestablishment by seducing Warner—and then putting a bullet in his shoulder. But as she’ll learn in <i>Destroy Me</i>, Warner is not that easy to get rid of...<br /><br />Back at the base and recovering from his near-fatal wound, Warner must do everything in his power to keep his soldiers in check and suppress any mention of a rebellion in the sector. Still as obsessed with Juliette as ever, his first priority is to find her, bring her back, and dispose of Adam and Kenji, the two traitors who helped her escape. But when Warner’s father, The Supreme Commander of The Reestablishment, arrives to correct his son’s mistakes, it’s clear that he has much different plans for Juliette. Plans Warner simply cannot allow.<br /><br />Set after <i>Shatter Me</i> and before its forthcoming sequel, <i>Unravel Me</i>, <i>Destroy Me</i> is a novella told from the perspective of Warner, the ruthless leader of Sector 45.</span>

<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/38506416-riley"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1463949780i/38506416._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/38506416-riley">Riley</a>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You don't need to read this in order to read the next one, it is just a novella. And the order of the entire series, including the two novellas is:<br/><br/>#1 <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You don't need to read this in order to read the next one, it is just a novella. And the order of the entire series, including the two novellas is:<br /><br />#1 Shatter me<br />#1.5 (Novella) Destroy me<br />#2 Unravel me<br />#2.5 (Novella) Fracture me<br />#3 Ignite me<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1668088698" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3372230956625587988">5/5 heartbreaking stars.<br/>This novella is a must-read for anyone reading the series.<br/>While reading, you may feel how much you cannot contain Warner's feelings. This person is a mess of disappointment, bad influence, abuse and anger from the world around him. So much pain, shame, hatred- all in a 19 year-old boy. Many readers hated Warner in the first book. I didn’t. I knew -felt- how many walls were around him, walls he had built. I noticed that his behavior was a red light. In this novella you see</span>
  <span id="freeText3372230956625587988" style="display:none">5/5 heartbreaking stars.<br />This novella is a must-read for anyone reading the series.<br />While reading, you may feel how much you cannot contain Warner's feelings. This person is a mess of disappointment, bad influence, abuse and anger from the world around him. So much pain, shame, hatred- all in a 19 year-old boy. Many readers hated Warner in the first book. I didn’t. I knew -felt- how many walls were around him, walls he had built. I noticed that his behavior was a red light. In this novella you see exactly how he does it. How he builds his walls, how he suffers. You understand what was behind every decision and every move he made in the first book.<br /><br />Beware, my friends, after this novella you won't have a way back. You won't be able to resist your love for Warner. Because this kid will break your heart to pieces.</span>

I admired her, envied her composure--her steadiness in the face of all she'd been forced to endure. <i>I don't know that I understood what it was, exactly, I was feeling at the time, but I knew I wanted her all to myself.</i><br><br><b>2.</b> Her face keeps cropping up, her journal taunting me from its place in my pocket. And I shot him in the forehead because I thought it'd be kinder than ripping him to pieces by hand.<br><br><b>4.</b> I almost forget that she still hates me, despite how hard I've fallen for her. <br>And I've fallen. <br>So hard.</blockquote></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1114881835" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1070893728189664237"><b>*3.5 stars*</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416889294i/12100387.jpg' width='400' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Possibly, the reason why I am not loving this as much as everyone else – even though I still enjoyed it – is because I’ve finished the Shatter Me trilogy weeks ago and only now decided to pick this #1.5 novella up.<br/><br/>It may not have been the most intelligent thing to do, but, in my defence, novellas are not my favorite types of reads and I prefer to leave them be, so they don’t risk ruining characters or…some scenes for me. Like it happened somehow with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15754052.Roar_and_Liv__Under_the_Never_Sky___0_5_' title='Roar and Liv (Under the Never Sky, #0.5) by Veronica Rossi' rel='nofollow noopener'>Roar and Liv</a>…<br/><br/>This was good though.</span>
  <span id="freeText1070893728189664237" style="display:none"><b>*3.5 stars*</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1416889294i/12100387.jpg" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Possibly, the reason why I am not loving this as much as everyone else – even though I still enjoyed it – is because I’ve finished the Shatter Me trilogy weeks ago and only now decided to pick this #1.5 novella up.<br><br>It may not have been the most intelligent thing to do, but, in my defence, novellas are not my favorite types of reads and I prefer to leave them be, so they don’t risk ruining characters or…some scenes for me. Like it happened somehow with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15754052.Roar_and_Liv__Under_the_Never_Sky___0_5_" title="Roar and Liv (Under the Never Sky, #0.5) by Veronica Rossi" rel="nofollow noopener">Roar and Liv</a>…<br><br>This was good though. Not perfect, but good enough.<br><br>I just couldn’t stay away. After finishing book #3, I needed more.<br><br>I needed Warner Warner Warner. (See, this author is wearing off on me….*wink* * wink*)<br><br>And Warner is what I got.<br><br>But also a lot of Juliette. Which I did not want. Of course, I was ready to hear him explicitly tell us about how much he misses her and wants to find her again, but not to actually read bits of her notebook! I thought this was supposed to focus on Warner. Hmmm.<br><br>The writing is great, as always, and giving us the possibility to easily enter into the story and comprehend the characters.<br><br>However, I found Warner to be a little cheap. I mean, he narrated the story, so, technically, wasn’t he supposed to open up and tell us <em>every single thing</em> that was onto his mind? Because he did keep some things secret. Which I found frustrating.<br><br>For instance:<br><blockquote>My research had led me to her files by pure accident. Coincidence. I did not seek her out in search of a weapon; I never had. Far before I’d ever seen her on film, and far, far before I ever spoke a word to her, I had been researching something else. For something else.<br><strong>My motives were my own.</strong>
</blockquote><br>Care to maybe <em>share</em> these motives in question with us? I know the actual answer to what he wanted with Juliette after all, since I indeed read the third book in which it is explained, but I think this is being very evasive and not really honest with us. Would I have been a reader who had just finished book #1 and craved for the second one, I think I would have liked to know what those motives are.<br><br>Warner’s love for Juliette is, I believe, even more presently described and related to in this novella than in the last book, which I find surprising. Only for that fact alone, I would recommend reading this. Also, I quickly realized that the novella does make this (former – or not – depending) antihero, with every new chapter, endearing to us. It simply is impossible to still look at him and see a cold hearted and sadistic person after reading this.<br><br>Truth be told, I will never forget him. <em>Ever.</em></span>
  <a data-text-id="1070893728189664237" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <blockquote>“I almost forget that she still hates me, despite how hard I've fallen for her.<br/>And I've fallen.<br/>So hard.<br/>I've hit </blockquote></b></i></span>

  <i>Re-Read : (13/02/2018)</i>

This book is so necessary if you're reading the Shatter Me trilogy, I think that will give you a new perspective of Warner and his personal story, you can't miss this one, of course it's a 5/5 Stars for me, always</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1518546931ra/25053703.gif" width="500" height="208" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>

</i><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I almost forget that she still hates me, despite how hard I've fallen for her.<br>And I've fallen.<br>So hard.<br>I've hit the ground.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><br><u>Oh Warner ! . I'm officially in love with this character !. This has been, Hard, Raw and Real ... So many feelings ...</u><br><br><br>I think this novella is one of the best I've read. This well thought out and recited, so that you can see the soul of the character, it's like, breaks his armor and we see Warner for what he really is, how he has arrived where it is and why.<br><br>This reading has come to my heart and I think it has been written by the author in a very intelligent way, no doubt , we understand many things that Warner has said and done in Shatter Me. And all those things made me love this character even more !.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I’ve come to believe that the most dangerous man in the world is the one who feels no remorse. The one who never apologizes and therefore seeks no forgiveness. Because in the end it is our emotions that make us week, not our actions.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><br>I have marveled reading the Warner's feelings toward Juliette! . It's just beautiful !. It is so real and sincere, the manifestation of him dreams, desires and darkest thoughts, has been brilliant; I really hope that at some point of the following book Juliette achieves to know all there in the head and in the heart of Warner, because, really girls!, who would resist !.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“She is a soft, deadly creature. Kind and timid and terrifying. She's completely out of control and has no idea what she's capable of. And even though she hates me, I can't help but be fascinated by her. I'm enchanted by her pretend-innocence; jealous, even, of the power she wields so unwittingly. I want so much to be a part of her world. I want to know what it's like to be in her mind, to feel what she feels. It seems a tremendous weight to carry.<br>And now she's out there, somewhere, unleashed on society.<br>What a beautiful disaster.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1458063518ra/18440068.gif" width="500" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>Officially I hate Warner's father , he has so much power over his son and knows exactly how to make him suffer and he achieved disarm him so easily only with words. I think he may have a greater role in the plot during the next book and that makes me very nervous.<br><br>So I'm excited to start with Unravel Me ... I'm looking for a lot in this next book, I hope it to reach my expectations.:)<br><br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“This girl is destroying me.”</blockquote>
  </b>

<div id="review_663192620" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/663192620" />
    <a title="Regan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19645927-regan"><img alt="Regan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437809914p2/19645927.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

But I always feel like novella are "oh you can read it or not it doesn't matter"...but this one is a "YOU GOTTA READ IT AND UNDERSTAND WARNER." So I hereby say: I think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_' title='Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shatter Me</a> should've been dual narrated between Warner and Juliette! heh.   <span id="freeText14428865915595031850" style="display:none"><b>This is actually so so important to the series?!</b> And I'm mAD. I should've read it years ago! But I always feel like novella are "oh you can read it or not it doesn't matter"...but this one is a "YOU GOTTA READ IT AND UNDERSTAND WARNER." So I hereby say: I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a> should've been dual narrated between Warner and Juliette! heh. It would've made him seem like slightly a less creepy controlling sadistic cauliflower patch.<br /><br />Although tbh his obsession with Juliette is <i>still creepy</i>. When a girl says no, guess what?? SHE MEANS NO. Go sit down Warner.<br /><br />But I do feel sorry for him and he is scared (and reminds me a little of Cardan from The Cruel Prince?!) and ajfdklasd that he tries to protect things like smol children and then feeds lost dogs pastries and just...<b>a novella of quality content tbh.</b> I just think the disconnect between Warner's inner-self vs what he presents to the world needed to be better crafted. It makes <i>sense</i> what he's doing and how Juliette would see him. But I think we needed more hints in Shatter Me.<br /><br />ANYWAY. WARNER IS SOFT™.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060907840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6697596950937406197"><b>Warning: Do not read if you didn't read "Shatter Me" and don't want to be spoiled?! *lol*</b><br/><br/>I'm not quite sure if an additional short story to a series can really spoil you, but I thought I might warn you just in case! ;-P<br/>But then again the only people who will read this will be people who loved the series so umm.... We're good?! *lol*<br/><br/><b>Anywayyyyyyy!</b><br/><br/>First of all: I already liked Warner in “Shatter me” and to read his POV in “Destroy me” only caused me to love him even more! XD<br/><br/>I <b>L.O.V.E.</b> Warner and I </span>
  <span id="freeText6697596950937406197" style="display:none"><b>Warning: Do not read if you didn't read "Shatter Me" and don't want to be spoiled?! *lol*</b><br /><br />I'm not quite sure if an additional short story to a series can really spoil you, but I thought I might warn you just in case! ;-P<br />But then again the only people who will read this will be people who loved the series so umm.... We're good?! *lol*<br /><br /><b>Anywayyyyyyy!</b><br /><br />First of all: I already liked Warner in “Shatter me” and to read his POV in “Destroy me” only caused me to love him even more! XD<br /><br />I <b>L.O.V.E.</b> Warner and I want to hug him and heal his broken heart! Gosh! That poor boy! That lovely ruined and lonely little thing! To read what he thinks, what he feels and to know that Juliette’s written words and actions destroyed him… It was just too much to bear! T_T<br />I hated to read how much he struggled and how broken he truly is and I really really really hope that Juliette will give him a chance to win her heart. &gt;_&lt; His love for her is so intense that it actually hurt and I don’t even know how he’s able to get up each and every day. I mean, hell she shot him and considering his feelings this must have hurt at least as much as the wound! =(<br /><br />Well anyway! I liked his relationship with Delalieu and I hated his father! With a fierce passion! *grrr*<br />That scene where he almost choked his own son? Gosh how much I despise him! <br />Can anyone get rid of this man in the next few books? *hires Celaena*<br /><br />Since I’m a sucker for quotes I’m going to end this review with the ones I liked the most:<br /><br /><i>The things I said to her.<br />A tight breath.<br />The way I touched her.<br />My jaw tenses.<br />If it were nothing but sexual attraction I’m sure I would not suffer such unbearable humiliation. But I wanted so much more than her body.</i><br /><br />Yesh, you wanted to love her and she shot you! Dang it! T_T<br /><br /><i>“I drop the bread back onto my plate. “My opinions,” I say to him, quietly this time, “should not so easily break your own. Stand by your convictions. Form clear and logical arguments. Even if I disagree.”</i><br /><br />I adored him for that sentence alone! XD<br /><br /><i>“His hand closes around my throat.<br />The movement is so rough and violent I’m almost relieved. Some part of me always hopes he’ll go through with it; that maybe this time he’ll actually let me die. But he never does. It never lasts.<br />Torture is not torture when there’s any hope of relief.”</i><br /><br />That moment killed me, I swear! &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><i>“I did not bring her on base to exploit her ability. And I certainly did not expect to fall for her in the process. <br />But these truths and my real motivations will be buried with me.”</i><br /><br />Jeez! Hopefully not!!!<br /><br /><i>“A look into her mind.<br />And though the anticipation is killing me, I’m also acutely aware of just how badly this might backfire. I’m suddenly not sure I ever want to know. And yet I do. I definitely do.”</i><br /><br />Warner is so torn it’s almost painful! XD<br /><br /><i>“On the battlefield, I’m able to disconnect myself from the motions I’ve been taught to memorize. I’ve developed a reputation as a cold, unfeeling monster wo fears nothing and cares for less.<br />But this is all very deceiving.<br />Because the truth is, I am nothing but a coward.”</i><br /><br />You’re brave Warner! So brave! Don’t let anyone tell you any different!!!<br /><br /><i>“But there are some things I do not forgive.<br />I don’t consider myself a moral man. I do not philosophize about life or bother with the laws and principles that govern most people. I do not pretend to know the difference between right and wrong. But I do live by a certain kind of code. And sometimes, I think, you have to learn how to shoot first.”</i><br /><br />It was so sad that all his efforts had been in vain, but he’s trying to be a good person and that counts for something! =)<br /><br /><i>“Love is a heartless bastard.<br />I’m driving myself insane.”</i><br /><br />Warner you truly destroyed me… in the best possible way! <br /><br />And with that sentence <br />my review actually ends! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6697596950937406197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer10235451966932743469"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519315311ra/25105060.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i> “Sometimes I wish I could step outside of myself for a while. <br/>I want to leave this worn body behind, but my chains are too many, my weights too heavy. <br/>This life is all that’s left of me. <br/>And I know I won’t be able to meet myself in the mirror for the rest of the day.” </i> <br/><br/>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>This is a novella in Warner’s point of view where we see what’s going on in his mind after Juliette shot him. We get to meet Warner’s dad who is the real monster in the family. <br/>We see Warner’s true and deep feelings</span>
  <span id="freeText10235451966932743469" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519315311ra/25105060.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i> “Sometimes I wish I could step outside of myself for a while. <br>I want to leave this worn body behind, but my chains are too many, my weights too heavy. <br>This life is all that’s left of me. <br>And I know I won’t be able to meet myself in the mirror for the rest of the day.” </i> <br><br>Story ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>This is a novella in Warner’s point of view where we see what’s going on in his mind after Juliette shot him. We get to meet Warner’s dad who is the real monster in the family. <br>We see Warner’s true and deep feelings for Juliette. <br><br>Characters ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>There’s not one character in this story more interesting than Warner. <br>After the first book “Shatter me” it’s obvious that Tahereh Mafi wants to make Warner the villain of the story. But he is so much more and I love that about him. <br>He is my absolute favorite ♥️ <br>He is intelligent, strong and supportive. He’s sad and hates the world he lives in. <br>He sees that is wrong. That the reestablishment isn’t doing a good job. <br>He can’t to anything about it. <br>But still he tries to do little good things, kind things for people. <br><br>Writing style ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br>I love Tahereh Mafis writing style so much. Especially in this book where we see Juliette’s notebook in the time when she was in the Asylum. Where we see Warner’s thoughts and feelings so openly presented.</span>

  <span id="freeText11377474709081958341" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE! <s>FUCKING</s>AWESOME UPDATE!♥</b><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://shelf-life.ew.com/2012/10/05/tahereh-mafi-destroy-me-trailer-exclusive/">http://shelf-life.ew.com/2012/10/05/t...</a><br>Official <b>BOOK TRAILER</b> and an excerpt of this book.^ <br>Lets just say, I <i>died</i> after watching the trailer. Her writing was beyond epic in this one. This author just <b>NAILED</b> it. You deserve a standing ovation girl! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/384492.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Talking about the book, Destroy Me shows the side of Warner, you have never seen before and everybody will be taken by surprise in the end. His feelings about Juliette are so intense. Lets just say, my mind was literally screaming and it just makes me Team Warner more. You feel sorry for him and in the end, I was like, "Go boy, get your girl from Adam! You deserve more here!"<br><br>Some scenes which I loved:<br>(1) Him dreaming about Juliette.<br>(2) When he is reading from her diary.<br>(3) Dreaming about Juliette again.<br>(4) Playing with the dog.<br><br>Best line:<br><p>
  <i>"That this girl would know exactly how to shatter me."</i>
</p><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/337959.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">^^<br>I <b>loved loved loved</b> this book, 5/5 stars. I am dying, literally, to read Unravel Me. Excited. Period. <br>Au revoir, My fellow Warner lovers! :D</span>

        <a title="She-who-must-not-be-named " class="user" itemprop="url" name="She-who-must-not-be-named " href="/user/show/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named">She-who-must-not-be-named </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=novella">novella</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106473614-she-who-must-not-be-named?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3339011004" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4752426475672257159">I most definitely needed this novella. It shows Warner's perspective of things and his complicated yet heartfelt feelings for Juliette giving us a deep insight into his character complex. He may not be a good person, but we get to know that the world wasn't good to him either, and I rooted for him profoundly. The author also shares with the readers his past showing that he is not the monster he is thought to be, it was all a facade and that deep down, he has feelings too and seeing Juliette esca</span>
  <span id="freeText4752426475672257159" style="display:none">I most definitely needed this novella. It shows Warner's perspective of things and his complicated yet heartfelt feelings for Juliette giving us a deep insight into his character complex. He may not be a good person, but we get to know that the world wasn't good to him either, and I rooted for him profoundly. The author also shares with the readers his past showing that he is not the monster he is thought to be, it was all a facade and that deep down, he has feelings too and seeing Juliette escape like that shattered them.<br />All in all, it was amazing getting to know more about Warner, his dark feelings, his past struggles and he's definitely the most interesting character I've ever read about.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2118346984655596435" style="display:none"><u>4.25 SHE WILL CHOOSE ME. ★'s</u><br><br><i>“Watching her talk to someone else made me crazy. I was jealous. Ridiculous. I wanted her to know me; I wanted her to talk to me. And I felt it then: this strange, inexplicable sense that she might be the only person in the world I could really care about.”</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521269490i/25226814._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I can't believe I did not read this before now! In all honesty, I usually don't enjoy these short filler story's all that much. They usually bore me, there for I usually just skip them unless, I want a quick read. I am so happy, I chose to read this. If I thought I was intrigued by Warner in Shatter Me, I have fallen so completely for him now. Just like I thought, there is just so much more to him then what meets the eye. He is not all malice and heartlessness, it's what he was taught and molded into. But if given the chance, people might just surprise you. I loved that we got a chance to be inside Warner's head. It's always refreshing when we get insight into another character's mind and a look into their soul. I love complex character so much. <div id="review_1655366288" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655366288" />
    <a title="Mariah of the Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29456303-mariah-of-the-night-court"><img alt="Mariah of the Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585943105p2/29456303.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655366288?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mariah of the Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mariah of the Night Court" href="/user/show/29456303-mariah-of-the-night-court">Mariah of the Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655366288" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5381574843067659521"><b>WARNER MY LOVE.</b><br/><br/><b>***Contains Spoilers***</b><br/><br/><b>I HAVE NEVER READ A NOVELLA SO QUICKLY AND INTENSELY LIKE THIS IN MY LIFE.</b><br/><br/>The whole entire 109 pages were from Warner's point of view and made me love him more than I already do. And he thinks about Juliette a ton, which may sound a bit obsessive, but it still makes me all happy inside. The ways in which he thinks about her though are so, like, I can't even put it into words. Even though Juliette hates him, I still ship her and Warner together.<br/><br/><i>“That this gir</i></span>
  <span id="freeText5381574843067659521" style="display:none"><b>WARNER MY LOVE.</b><br /><br /><b>***Contains Spoilers***</b><br /><br /><b>I HAVE NEVER READ A NOVELLA SO QUICKLY AND INTENSELY LIKE THIS IN MY LIFE.</b><br /><br />The whole entire 109 pages were from Warner's point of view and made me love him more than I already do. And he thinks about Juliette a ton, which may sound a bit obsessive, but it still makes me all happy inside. The ways in which he thinks about her though are so, like, I can't even put it into words. Even though Juliette hates him, I still ship her and Warner together.<br /><br /><i>“That this girl would know exactly how to shatter me.”</i> <br /><br />Warner becomes such a misunderstood character as you slowly learn why he is the way he is, and the main reason for that is because of his father. He's been abused all his childhood for never being good enough and constantly put down for showing even a bit of empathy towards someone. His father taught him to never empathize with anyone and to take what you want and destroy anything that gets in the way. Warner's father even started to choke him while he was recovering from his bullet wound in the hospital bed, and then continued scolding him for being a stupid and weak ruler. What a fucked up asshole.<br /><br />Throughout this entire novella, I just wanted to reach in and pull Warner in for a hug. He's hates his life and how he's the one who built it out of fear, just as his father taught him. I was seriously going to cry for him.<br /><br /><i>“People seldom realize that they tell lies with their lips and truths with their eyes all the time.”</i> <br /><br />I loved how the real reason why Warner shot Flecher was explained. Warner knew his guard was abusing his wife and three small children. His wife even took a beating so hard that she miscarried her child. I'm glad that Warner killed that guard because of that knowledge. But, when his father found out, he told him that traitorous guards bring about traitorous families and that they should be killed as well. And they were, at his father's hand. A mother and her three small children, barely reaching the age of ten. My heart broke along with Warner's.<br /><br />When Warner searched Juliette's room and found her notebook, I just kind of stilled and stopped breathing because I knew that when he read it, I was never going to look at the future Warner and Juliette scenes the same way again. He most likely felt the same way but 100x more. And then he sat at the edge of her bed, opened the notebook, and began to read.<br /><br /><i>“I’ve come to believe that the most dangerous man in the world is the one who feels no remorse. The one who never apologizes and therefore seeks no forgiveness. Because in the end it is our emotions that make us week, not our actions.”</i> <br /><br />He read Juliette's deepest, most personal thoughts she wrote down while she stayed in the asylum. It was so sad how she described her life alone without anyone to find comfort with and how she was constantly being pushed away by the ones she was closest to. Her own family didn't want anything to do with her. She hated her life.<br /><br />There were so many similarities with how Warner and Juliette were brought up throughout their lives and how they were constantly met with emotional and physical abuse. Warner was hated by his family because he wan't feared enough and Juliette was hated by her family because she was too feared. It broke my heart how much they really share with each other. They were never good enough. <br /><br /><i>“I almost forget that she still hates me, despite how hard I've fallen for her.<br />And I've fallen.<br />So hard.<br />I've hit the ground.”</i><br /><br />Now that I have a full understanding of Warner, I will never look at him the same way again. I'm glad of it though, because deep down, he is a selfless and empathetic person. These hidden qualities just need to be tempted to surface. It's going to be interesting to see how he develops in the next two books and I'm looking forward to it. <br /><br /><i>“My mind is a warehouse of carefully organized human emotions.<br />I lock away the things that do not serve me.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="5381574843067659521" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2660336140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15144362637323729058"><b>4 stars</b> <b>
  <blockquote>Love is a heartless bastard. I’m driving myself insane.</blockquote>
</b> <br/>After reading <i>Destroy Me</i>, I am completely softened to Warner. I wasn’t sure if I would like him, but there was something in the first book that intrigued me. After reading this, I can most definitely say I understand him much better and I truly do like him. Warner isn’t perfect, but he’s not the man I thought he was. He’s so much more. I loved being in his head and seeing his thoughts about Juliette, and his relationship with hi</span>
  <span id="freeText15144362637323729058" style="display:none"><b>4 stars</b> <b>
  <blockquote>Love is a heartless bastard. I’m driving myself insane.</blockquote>
</b> <br />After reading <i>Destroy Me</i>, I am completely softened to Warner. I wasn’t sure if I would like him, but there was something in the first book that intrigued me. After reading this, I can most definitely say I understand him much better and I truly do like him. Warner isn’t perfect, but he’s not the man I thought he was. He’s so much more. I loved being in his head and seeing his thoughts about Juliette, and his relationship with his dad. I feel like he really sees Juliette. He sees her loneliness, her struggle, and he can relate to it. I can’t wait to read more of this series and see where it takes him! <br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>Friendship is not a thing I have ever experienced. Not as a child, and not as I am now. Except. One month ago, I met the exception to this rule. There has been one person who’s ever looked me directly in the eye. The same person who’s spoken to me with no filter; someone who’s been unafraid to show anger and real, raw feeling in my presence; the only one who’s ever dared to challenge me, to raise her voice to me—<br /><br />She is a soft, deadly creature. Kind and timid and terrifying. She’s completely out of control and has no idea what she’s capable of. And even though she hates me, I can’t help but be fascinated by her. I’m enchanted by her pretend-innocence; jealous, even, of the power she wields so unwittingly. I want so much to be a part of her world. I want to know what it’s like to be in her mind, to feel what she feels. It seems a tremendous weight to carry.</blockquote>
  </b>
</i></span>

<div id="review_353887343" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353887343" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353887343?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=shorty">shorty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353887343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6134821482579032285">Oh, my dear Warner, I love you so much it hurts. (4.5 stars)<br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/tahereh-mafi/review-destroy-me.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381655i/739023.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I saw right through him.<br/>You see, I love it when my heart is right.. and right now it still loves Warner to pieces.<br/>Yes, he’s the bad guy.<br/>No, he doesn’t need to convince me otherwise.<br/><br/>If I liked this amazing and complex character in Shatter Me, well now I feel like I’ve been bewitched by him, his dark mind, his fears, and his struggle. I repeat, Warner is not a good person, the world didn’t make him good, the world was not good to him </span>
  <span id="freeText6134821482579032285" style="display:none">Oh, my dear Warner, I love you so much it hurts. (4.5 stars)<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/tahereh-mafi/review-destroy-me.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380381655i/739023.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I saw right through him.<br>You see, I love it when my heart is right.. and right now it still loves Warner to pieces.<br>Yes, he’s the bad guy.<br>No, he doesn’t need to convince me otherwise.<br><br>If I liked this amazing and complex character in Shatter Me, well now I feel like I’ve been bewitched by him, his dark mind, his fears, and his struggle. I repeat, Warner is not a good person, the world didn’t make him good, the world was not good to him either.. But deep down he had feelings, and I loved the sound of his breaking heart..<br><br>Also, seeing the difference in writing, somehow all the confusion and struggle form the first book made sense. Juliette and her disturbed mind mean so much more to me now that I see inside Warner’s head, his calculated (almost sophisticated) way of thinking, his elegant way of speaking.<br><br>God, how different these voices can be: Warner and Juliette. I love what the author did here, how she could bring to life such fleshed-out characters, so different but so well defined. This is exactly what I like about an author: to be able to convince me that I’m reading the character’s words and not her/his own.<br><br>Also, I can now appreciate so much better Shatter Me, because I understood a few things I didn’t like back then:<br><br><i>1. The obsession with numbers.</i><br>Juliette counted her life in numbers, in breaths, so now it makes sense that she always wrote the numbers the way she did.. Her head is full of them – counting and counting, because that’s all that’s left of her. Warner on the other hand is building imaginary walls, securing his mind, emptying his heart when he needs to stay focused, when he needs to protect himself from the outside world.<br><br>He is in a difficult position being his father’s son, hating him so much but having to follow his path. In a way he is a prisoner to his world, the way Juliette is to hers. They don’t have much of a choice, do they, but they have so much in common.<br><br><i>2. The repetitions.</i><br>Juliette’s brain is quite disturbed. The world didn’t want her, so she spent so much time alone with the words floating around in her mind, obsessing and obsessing about things she couldn’t have. Now that I can see it from “above”, I can get a better picture of all that.. And yes, I admit, I might have been wrong. As disturbing as the repetition were, they were part of Juliette’s mind… I was reading her words and not the author’s.<br><br>Warner is the complete opposite. He has been in the center of attention, measuring his words, securing his thoughts, not giving away his feelings. He knows how to charm you, how to read you, how to convince you of everything he wants, because when words are not enough power can back them up quite nicely… and power is what he has plenty.<br><br><i>3. Adam</i><br>You know I didn’t like him that much and it made me sad the fact that the cliché seemed to happen: the good boy got the good girl. Wasn’t it such a fairytale?<br>Oh, you fooled me, Tahereh, yes you did!<br>I loved your beautiful writing in the beginning, but now I love you as an author, because if you can write such different characters with such different voices, then you deserve all the hype and then some more.<br><br>Still, taking a step back to think about it, it makes sense for Juliette to make that choice: Adam was the only one giving her freedom, not pushing her actions, but taking care of her. It was obvious that she would pick him to be her savior.<br>But now that she left behind a cage for another one, a side of the war for the opposite, will her claustrophobia suffocate her? Will she be the weapon both sides want her to be? Or will she want to break free?<br><br>Yes, I must confess that at this point I really hope for Juliette to choose Warner, and deep down this hope is the one making me want to read the next book. And I know that I might be wrong about all this, that I might get to be disappointed in the ending, but as long as I got to be in Warner’s mind for a just bit, as long as I got to see a different side of him, I will be happy.. Because I was right – he is the most interesting character in this story, and my love for him was not in vain.<br><br>Now, really.. I can’t wait for the next book. At the end of “Shatter Me” I was not convinced yet… I lost hope, but this tiny book gave it all back to me. I don’t trust Juliette to make the right decisions, but i trust the author to make this story glow.<br><br>Happy midnight reading!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/tahereh-mafi/review-destroy-me.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380339972i/696540.jpg" alt="" width="483" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i> * This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/tahereh-mafi/review-destroy-me.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a> </i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1446515979" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3065083007450039997">⚫ <b>
  <u>THIS IS NOT A REVIEW. THIS IS A STORY. A TRAGEDY.</u>
</b><br/><i>Years ago when I was only but a young - and fairly impressionable too, fairly- girl, I met a boy. Dark and beautiful he was, intense too, and I unwittingly fell in love with him. Abominably madly, completely in love with him. That chapter of my life's been over for almost 4 years now, almost 4 years the story's been over, and still I can't forget him.<b> I never will</b>.</i><br/><br/>✔ <u>
  <b>Reread. Again: Jan 31st/2016.</b>
</u><br/>Every time I reread this, I become more and</span>
  <span id="freeText3065083007450039997" style="display:none">⚫ <b>
  <u>THIS IS NOT A REVIEW. THIS IS A STORY. A TRAGEDY.</u>
</b><br><i>Years ago when I was only but a young - and fairly impressionable too, fairly- girl, I met a boy. Dark and beautiful he was, intense too, and I unwittingly fell in love with him. Abominably madly, completely in love with him. That chapter of my life's been over for almost 4 years now, almost 4 years the story's been over, and still I can't forget him.<b> I never will</b>.</i><br><br>✔ <u>
  <b>Reread. Again: Jan 31st/2016.</b>
</u><br>Every time I reread this, I become more and more convinced of one simple truth.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407195075ra/10654092.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(I hope my mother never finds this. She would die of heartbreak. I'm not just in love with a ghost, I'm in love with a ghost who never even lived.)<br><br><b>
  <u>AARON WARNER IS THE ONE.</u>
</b><br><br>I can hear you you know. YES YOU. You over there who keeps murmuring:<i>Oh would you get over him already?! Just move on.</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1451907391ra/17619241.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452177926ra/17656775.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I'll juuuust be forgetting you now<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452178007ra/17656789.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>To be honest, I don't even remember anything about this series apart from Aaron Warner. <b>Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner. Warner.</b><br>Now I know what you're thinking. And no, I am <u>NOT.</u><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1454207364ra/17931094.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Okay maybe I am. A teeny weeny bit. But Aaron is everything and I'll never have the luxury of fangirling to my full lunatic potential again. I am home alone and I intend to put this time to good use. Now excuse me while I go scream my voice to hoarseness. I'm going to fangirl myself into a neck brace. Toodaloo!<br><br>✔ <u>
  <b>Reread: Nov. 19th/2015</b>
</u><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>Dear Aaron,<br> These are the things I know about you, things you've shared, things you've said, and things I just know, things I will not be sharing with anyone else--<br>I love you. I loved you from the very first page of your story. The story of you, the boy with the green eyes and matching green ring. You said you don't seek redemption? You don't need sympathy? That's good Aaron, because I won't be the one to offer you any. I saw you then, before the blood and before the gun that opened you up and spilled your words. And I see you now. You're neither evil nor good, you're made of things too complex and colorful to be condemned to dreary frames of black and white, too ordinary to be called extraordinary, and still too extraordinary to just be ordinary. You're my most worrisome puzzle. And yet I love you more than I love<s> Harry Potter</s> Percy Jackson. Let's say that were enough to make real bones grow, and cause real blood to flow and fill a real heart with love that's <s>equal</s> far more greater than mine. Let's pretend I could love you out of your world and into mine. Let's pretend I'm not crazy for writing this.<br><br>I watched a movie once of a woman who was so obsessed with Mr. Darcy that she lived by standards built around the essence of him. She lived chasing the idea of him, so consumed by her fantasies of him and the world he lived in. So she drifted from disappointment to disappointment, from one unsatisfied state to another, so apart from reality. And I wonder, will that woman ever be me?<br>No, I think not. I have my feet planted too firmly on the ground for that, but I just want to say;<br>After all these years, I still compare every boy I read about to you.<br><b>"He doesn't talk like Aaron.<br>He doesn't have presence like Aaron<br>He isn't a beautiful mess like Aaron<br>He isn't as bewildering as Aaron <br>He isn't as intense as Aaron<br>He isn't Aaron."</b><br><br>So if you ever do materialize, come find me.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>I just had to reread this after someone--I refuse to name names--got me excited about this series again. I can't believe I never wrote about this! Thank you Giulia! Oops...</b> <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3065083007450039997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U7l7dSzJYi4w1Qm1uTpx2cngBxI4ykuDH+V0WpT+wVCYkugq2vWd4mia0szmJpSAs3NXw8VHLboTCkmd7BVVIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wa52c02NKnWg/9DM0auev8LGpuTIZV7fb7+5dYt7QWcKheUsu7HVufiwC7WOt3vmuFX2NTXoOOZjUISy85DVFw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer4435355832064764207">Tahereh Mafi is the <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of the <i>Shatter Me</i> series. She was born in a small city somewhere in Connecticut and currently resides in Santa Monica, California with her husband, fellow author <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3046613.Ransom_Riggs' title='Ransom Riggs' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ransom Riggs</a>. She can usually be found over-caffeinated and stuck in a book. <i>Shatter Me</i> is her first series, with television rights optioned by ABC Signature Studios; <i>Fur</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4435355832064764207" style="display:none">Tahereh Mafi is the <i>New York Times</i> and <i>USA Today</i> bestselling author of the <i>Shatter Me</i> series. She was born in a small city somewhere in Connecticut and currently resides in Santa Monica, California with her husband, fellow author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3046613.Ransom_Riggs" title="Ransom Riggs" rel="nofollow noopener">Ransom Riggs</a>. She can usually be found over-caffeinated and stuck in a book. <i>Shatter Me</i> is her first series, with television rights optioned by ABC Signature Studios; <i>Furthermore</i>, her first middle grade novel, is on shelves now, and <i>Whichwood</i>, its darker companion, will be on shelves November 14, 2017.</span>
